    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1117836947" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16334716998790999755">UPDATE (2017/06/21): This manga is now being printed in English!! I am now able to share my love for it with the world in a tangible form. I read and posted this review 2 and a half years ago and Punpun is still in the top two best comics I've ever read (tied with Watchmen). I read it about three years ago and I still think about it daily. Incredible manga. If I could afford to buy the volumes in person, I would be rereading it.<br/><br/><br/>It has taken me months to gather my feelings enough to formulate a c</span>
  <span id="freeText16334716998790999755" style="display:none">UPDATE (2017/06/21): This manga is now being printed in English!! I am now able to share my love for it with the world in a tangible form. I read and posted this review 2 and a half years ago and Punpun is still in the top two best comics I've ever read (tied with Watchmen). I read it about three years ago and I still think about it daily. Incredible manga. If I could afford to buy the volumes in person, I would be rereading it.<br /><br /><br />It has taken me months to gather my feelings enough to formulate a coherent review.<br />Absolute genius. Seems a little flowery of an opinion but allow me to explain why.<br />I'm not at all a manga person. I have never attempted it before this one because all manga I've seen at my local book store is either extremely violent action-based manga or those ones with the girls with big boobs on the cover. My boyfriend had to convince me for ages to actually try out Punpun. I went in with very low expectations because I'd stereotyped the entire genre as something I'd hate.<br />But I could not put this down (figuratively, of course- it's online-only). I have never experienced such a twisted coming-of-age story and, my god, was it brilliant. The transition Punpun goes though as he grows up is one that a lot of people can relate to in some way. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Maybe not entirely. I hope not. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I did not at all expect such a powerful manga. Each character/storyline represents something different psychologically and there are some incredibly dark themes that drained me emotionally. This is the kind of book(s) that leaves you thinking about it for days. Months, in my case. <br />Lastly, The art was beautifully done and executed perfectly. I loved the touch of depicting Punpun as a bird as well as a few other shapes and sizes as his emotions changed.<br />In short, this manga is a beautiful work of art and I wish it was printed in English. I would buy every volume.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16334716998790999755" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13064236218732217882">How does guilt mold and guide you? How do your memories prevent you from reconciling with your present? How do you get stuck focused on what's behind, missing what's right next to you? How does your family sculpt you despite your fierce desire against it? Promises you end up not keeping, against others, against yourself. How long do you wait until you move on, and how do you move on?<br/><br/>Where do you find meaning and who do you appoint as your guiding light? What if you you're the only one who sees t</span>
  <span id="freeText13064236218732217882" style="display:none">How does guilt mold and guide you? How do your memories prevent you from reconciling with your present? How do you get stuck focused on what's behind, missing what's right next to you? How does your family sculpt you despite your fierce desire against it? Promises you end up not keeping, against others, against yourself. How long do you wait until you move on, and how do you move on?<br /><br />Where do you find meaning and who do you appoint as your guiding light? What if you you're the only one who sees that light?<br /><br />What happens when you force yourself to blend in, abandoning your true identity?<br /><br />A dark story with enough characters to explore all of the above and then some. Exquisite drawings that capture both the deep characters and the living city they inhabit. They confidently veer off their arresting realism when the story demands it, from the inspired fluidity of the protagonist's self-image to the occasional, reality-bending visions of key characters.<br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9206058346346987114"> This manga was really good. Compared to all the other mangas that I've read, Oyasumi Punpun was the best. This manga changed my point of view on growing up. And it helps you realize what the world really is. It's crazy, yet beautiful.   <span id="freeText9206058346346987114" style="display:none"> This manga was really good. Compared to all the other mangas that I've read, Oyasumi Punpun was the best. This manga changed my point of view on growing up. And it helps you realize what the world really is. It's crazy, yet beautiful. This manga taught me a lot about love, life, people,death, and depression. It made me cry, and feel things that I haven't felt before. It's somewhat heartbreaking. This manga has also taught me that once you meet someone, your paths never really part. Even if things are bad, its going to get good at one point in your life, Oyasumi Punpun helped me notice that too. Overall Oyasumi Punpun was a terrific read, and it can change the way you view life.</span>

<div id="review_2915697419" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2915697419" />
    <a title="Salman Farisi Prasad" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/62879918-salman-farisi-prasad"><img alt="Salman Farisi Prasad" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1501513121p2/62879918.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2915697419?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Salman Farisi Prasad" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Salman Farisi Prasad" href="/user/show/62879918-salman-farisi-prasad">Salman Farisi Prasad</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/62879918-salman-farisi-prasad?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/62879918-salman-farisi-prasad?shelf=mango">mango</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2915697419" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2262634722443604507">There is a reason to be able to love and hate Inio Asano’s “Goodnight Punpun”. The reason I love it is that it depicted how the pain of living is, how realistic yet absurd a depression is, and how crisis our existential. On the other hand, the reason I hate it is because of the main character, Punpun Onodera, is a nothing, blankness, coward, without knowing the reason why he exists. When I first saw this on MyAnimeList, in the top-rated manga. Of all the manga on the list, this caught me a lot; </span>
  <span id="freeText2262634722443604507" style="display:none">There is a reason to be able to love and hate Inio Asano’s “Goodnight Punpun”. The reason I love it is that it depicted how the pain of living is, how realistic yet absurd a depression is, and how crisis our existential. On the other hand, the reason I hate it is because of the main character, Punpun Onodera, is a nothing, blankness, coward, without knowing the reason why he exists. When I first saw this on MyAnimeList, in the top-rated manga. Of all the manga on the list, this caught me a lot; although it’s hard to think why I just read it now. And now, “Goodnight Punpun” really deserves to be in the list of the best manga of all time. Sadly, a lot of people don’t really know about this.<br /><br />“Goodnight Punpun” is a dark comedy and a black satire manga. It’s possibly one of the most depressing and realistic manga you’ve come across. It’s a tale of coming-of-age, focusing on a boy, Punpun Punyama. We follow him all the way from his elementary school, stepping on the phase of adolescence, college, adulthood, until having a family. It’s probably not really your cup of tea because a lot of manga really highlighted such an unrealistic element. This manga is so special because it’s rather than a lot of things in its story, it’s a heavy impact for all of the readers. Psychological aspect in Punpun’s environment was so relatable to all of the people.<br /><br />At first, I don’t understand why a bird-like lives and exist in a human environment. Ridiculously, all the characters in this manga never realized it. But, there is a reason. First, Punpun’s character design depicted as glass and our reflection on the reader and even Punpun. It’s like portraying reader’s psychology from a plain design to growing up. Therefore, we recognize him better. We recognize it as a character, as a human being, as to how sick it was and suffering. Second, the manga isn’t just about a bird-like with two legs. However, Punpun’s family also uses these forms and caricatures. By utilizing this form, Punpun’s psychological state and symbolism emerged. How innocent is he? How dirty is he?<br /><br />It begins with Punpun was an elementary student, known had a crush on a newly transferred student in his school. After getting to know her name, Aiko Tanaka, for Punpun, it’s just a love of first sight. In Punpun’s point of view, he is rather a nil, besides his face and innocence about the world of maturity doesn’t make him if he is in puberty. He took the first step to Aiko as his friends. He just seems a normal boy. In his group, there are at least six character boys with the same activity like seeing porn magazines and testing their courage. Among all their friends, Seki and Kou are the most influential characters in the story.<br /><br />“Goodnight Punpun” is actually not only focused on Punpun in his childhood to adulthood. However, there are so many details on such things. We learn from many and various points of view, throughout the story, there is a lot of viewpoints from one to another character. As is the case, we don’t really know who Yuuichi Onodera really was and why he was so important in the manga. Likewise with Punpun’s mother, in the absence of Punpun, she is like an antagonist. But, we learned more about this character when we explore more. Yet, the entire plot isn’t just from Punpun’s cynical view but takes a wide range of us as the reader.<br /><br />For me, “Goodnight Punpun” is like Stanley Kubrick if he was a mangaka. If only he was a weeb, then the idea of ​​making this manga looks weird and absurd is such a great way. It’s true showing what emotions are, showing not just what we come across in Punpun’s mind, but also how a visual and language is so easy yet complex to explain. Regardless of his family and friends, resembling 2D birds-like with legs, the artwork is absurd, realistic, but there is a dream-like or surrealism.<br /><br />The backgrounds are so detailed as well as the character designs; and come think of it, this is adult manga. There are so many nudity and explicit content, rather than showing both of them as a fan service, it’s more you go into dark moments and situations. It’s like watching “Eyes Wide Shut“, which exploited its nudity, but the more you see it, the more you realize you don’t really enjoy it. The art is so realistic, hard to distinguish its events whether or not this is the same manga. It perfectly describes a lot of emotion, in one frame or panel or page, it repeats so many times like you don’t really know what to tell about.<br /><br />The manga seems more explore about God, as like Punpun also often talks about himself, his existence, and God. The more you read it, you would think this is just a nihilism from the image of God as a black afro guy. But, I see this two characters battle against Punpun’s head, like they both try to exist how bad and how depressing they are. Even though Punpun and God are like the same two characters, there is nothing to emphasize if they both exist in the same place. But, I prefer to call it two personalities or two alter egos, likes when he sees himself in the mirror but he doesn’t deny it’s really his face. And he never realized.<br /><br />Even from the Punpun journey, he finally learned a lot about how life is, how sex was, alcohol, the pain of losing, hiding behind the rock, all of it. “Goodnight Punpun” isn’t your typical happy story at all, just one chapter as much leaves an impact on its reader. Punpun questioning himself whether he makes a good decision in the first place. This is why I hate it because he isn’t actually perfect. Always hiding behind the rock, as he grows up, he realizes he has nothing but shelter. He has a lot of regret behind his family, friends, promises, little by little he forgets but also vice versa. When he fell, he just couldn’t remember anything else. Even though he does this in his narration, there has never been a dialogue between characters. Yet, it rather does it directly to the reader itself.<br /><br />Another reason why I hate Punpun is how he often exploded. When dogma and doctrine during his childhood were implanted by sexual matters, he was only concerned with himself. He never understanding others. Therefore, his friends left him and the people closest to him as well. He makes many worst decisions every day, every chapter. In his mind, sex is just his main food. It felt like even the same as our lives, make bad decisions every day as we do. However, we never know why, how, or for what reason we choose such a choice.<br /><br />This manga tells a lot about its characters, like about an occult club is one of the most interesting sub-plots in this manga. Not forgetting in exploring various sub-plots, there is also Seki and Kou as two best friends overlapping each other. It should be emphasized, all the sub-plots and minor characters are shown as triggers, cores, and relationships with the main story. Inio really utilizes this element. The story doesn’t only focus on the same theme but also deals with psychology, anxiety, and suicide attempts. The stories focus on these puzzles, in order to complete or unite everything, the main character must take the right choice. Sadly, not much too.<br /><br />“Goodnight Punpun” is about the pain of living, sadness, depression, anxiety, real life, and various stories in it. It might be one of the most depressing manga you don’t want to remember again when you finish reading it. It deals with so many themes, and lots of nudity, sex, and etc. Yet, it’s a manga people really overlooked even though the rating on MyAnimeList never changes anything. This manga is so underrated. And, it’s just the fact you don’t miss this manga.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2262634722443604507" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Shea" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/87025354-shea"><img alt="Shea" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1547634629p2/87025354.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2538889265?book_show_action=true">May 29, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shea" href="/user/show/87025354-shea">Shea</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2538889265&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2538889265" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8135644687563919654">4.5 ish. Parts of this manga were really good and then other parts were dogshit. Everything about Punpun and Aiko, Seki and Shizumi, specifically chapter 99 and 145, was amazing it was poignant and horrifically depressing, I was engaged with the story and cared about whatever was happening. But everything between Punpun’s childhood to meeting Aiko again was a slog (aside from Seki and Shizumi’s parts).<br/><br/>Specifically, I don’t find any of this manga entertaining. All the humor in this went over my l</span>
  <span id="freeText8135644687563919654" style="display:none">4.5 ish. Parts of this manga were really good and then other parts were dogshit. Everything about Punpun and Aiko, Seki and Shizumi, specifically chapter 99 and 145, was amazing it was poignant and horrifically depressing, I was engaged with the story and cared about whatever was happening. But everything between Punpun’s childhood to meeting Aiko again was a slog (aside from Seki and Shizumi’s parts).<br /><br />Specifically, I don’t find any of this manga entertaining. All the humor in this went over my level of caring. And there was humor... I think. Or at least aspects that were supposed to be funny (facial expressions, the caricatures, etc) and it just wasn’t. All the levity to this bleak plot is wasted on me which is why it took so long to read.<br /><br />Furthermore, the whole plot point about the world ending needed to go, I feel half the beauty in the realism was destroyed because of that “good vibrations” nonsense. It didn’t have anything to do with the general synopsis of Punpun’s life (we’ll get into Seki and that whole thing in a hot second) and and for me the whole “cults are bad” thing was done well enough with Aiko’s mom. For Seki and Shimizu it’s a little more complex — if it ended with Shimizu loosing his memories, then Seki confessing his feelings and running off with him into the sunset then I would have been satisfied. But it all just culminated into nothing except a bad time for Seki and a worse time for Shimizu.<br /><br />My only other quibble is that Seki and Shimizu should have been a couple. It would have made sense and they’re the only pair I really rooted for the entire time and could have developed in the same direction without introducing a girlfriend on Seki’s side out of nowhere.<br /><br />Other than that it was good, artwork was the goat.<br /><br />(Ngl, I think I liked Solanin more though, take that as you will.)</span>
  <a data-text-id="8135644687563919654" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7909113692500643850">So this place here that I'm writing a review will actually be the third time I've read Oyasumi Punpun.<br/><br/>And I would be lying if I said this would be the last time I would read it.<br/><br/>There's something raw in all of Asano's works, but I think this is the one that truly represents the pessimistic, fatalistic, nihilism in the world in a way that I honestly don't know if any other kind of media could accurately represent. It's painful yet cathartic in a way that I have a hard time putting into words.<br/><br/>It's </span>
  <span id="freeText7909113692500643850" style="display:none">So this place here that I'm writing a review will actually be the third time I've read Oyasumi Punpun.<br /><br />And I would be lying if I said this would be the last time I would read it.<br /><br />There's something raw in all of Asano's works, but I think this is the one that truly represents the pessimistic, fatalistic, nihilism in the world in a way that I honestly don't know if any other kind of media could accurately represent. It's painful yet cathartic in a way that I have a hard time putting into words.<br /><br />It's been nearly a decade since I discovered Punpun, but I don't know if I'll ever be able to forget him.</span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('2Vuddf0wDPxmjeczXrQKXvZwEanPEMaPVKN8u8EICYeuv9o3hXrwF60Ghx6DyAY7ft3RExLXSd9ZrTDNUTVgEQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('BYkQHhaYORHsKYQYj0sVMR19JunpbZB6HfjhusUXHCJybVdcbtLF+iei5DVSNxlUldDmUzSqHyoQ9q3MVSp1tA==')})
  }
//]]>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer3002134161679593245">Inio Asano (<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/10817895._____' title='浅野いにお' rel='nofollow noopener'>浅野いにお</a> Asano Inio, born September 22, 1980 in Ishioka, Ibaraki Prefecture, Japan) is a Japanese manga author. Asano created the acclaimed manga Solanin which was released as a feature film in Japan in April 2010, starring Aoi Miyazaki. He is known for his character driven, realist stories that range from slice of life stories to psychological horror. In 2001 he won the first prize in th</span>
  <span id="freeText3002134161679593245" style="display:none">Inio Asano (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/10817895._____" title="浅野いにお" rel="nofollow noopener">浅野いにお</a> Asano Inio, born September 22, 1980 in Ishioka, Ibaraki Prefecture, Japan) is a Japanese manga author. Asano created the acclaimed manga Solanin which was released as a feature film in Japan in April 2010, starring Aoi Miyazaki. He is known for his character driven, realist stories that range from slice of life stories to psychological horror. In 2001 he won the first prize in the GX competition for young manga artists.<br /><br />The Yomiuri Shimbun newspaper described him as "one of the voices of his generation."<br /><br />Instagram: <a href="https://www.instagram.com/asano_inio/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">asano_inio</a><br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inio_Asano">http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inio_Asano</a></span>
